Attributing Good Actions: Gratitude Over Command
Maturidi refutes Mu'tazila on attributing good deeds by command.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Maturidi argues that good actions should be attributed to Allah by gratitude and praise, not merely by command.

Core Idea
Attributing by gratitude distinguishes believers, while command applies to all.

In this passage, Maturidi and the Mu'tazila agree on a principle: nothing ugly is attributed to Allah. But they disagree on the basis for attributing good deeds. Maturidi argues that command, call, and strengthening are insufficient because they apply equally to believers and disbelievers. Instead, gratitude and praise are the proper basis, as they uniquely apply to believers.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once and then the translation. Notice the agreed principle and the two opposing views.
The passage is dense; take your time.
2
Identify the key positions
Find where the Mu'tazila say good actions are attributed to Allah (by command, call, strengthening) and where Maturidi responds (by gratitude and praise).
3
Understand the reasoning
Notice why Maturidi says gratitude is better: because command and strengthening apply to both believers and disbelievers, while gratitude distinguishes them.
The example of faith as a blessing illustrates this.
4
Reflect on the implication
Consider how this principle affects how we speak about Allah's role in our good deeds.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم نتفق والمعتزلة أن الله تعالى لا يضاف إليه شيء من الخلق أو أفعاله إلا من الوجه الذي لا يوهم القبح في الأسماء، ذلك فحقه أن ينفى عنه ذلك ويخرج على هذا مسائل: إحداها في وجه إضافة ما أضيف إلى الله من الخيرات، إنها من الله. قالت المعتزلة: يضاف إليه من أمر ودعا إليها وقوى عليها. وقلنا نحن: هذا من الإضافة، وإن كان حسنا فلا هذا يُراد بالإضافة إليه عند ذكر الأفعال، ولكن المراد الشكر والحمد له إذا ذكرت الأفعال. وقد يجوز الأول وهذا أولى؛ لأنه من حيث الأمر والدعاء والتقوية اشترك فيه المؤمن والكافر، ومن جهة الشكر والحمد يختلف، ومما يبين ذلك جواز القول المطلق: إن الإيمان نعم الله ومننه، وإن المؤمن قد أنعم الله عليه ومن، وأنه لولا فضل الله ما ذكى، ولمسه عذاب عظيم. ومن هذا الوجه لا يضاف إلى الله في الكافر، وإذا لم يذكر الأفعال فعلى الأمر، والله الموفق. ولهذا طعن الله من قال بالكتاب المبدل إنه من عند الله وبإضافتهم ونحوه، إنهم ادعوا الأمر بذلك، فبرأ الله نفسه عن ذلك، وأخبر أن ذلك من عمل الشيطان، وأنهم قالوا ذلك حسدا من عند أنفسهم، ولا قوة إلا بالله. ولا يجوز أيضا الفعل من حيث الأمر؛ لأنه ليس فيه إلا الالزام، وفي ذلك مؤن عظيمة لا يضاف إليه بذلك، بل من جهة الحمد والشكر كما قال: الله يَمُنُّ عَلَيْكُمْ، وقال: فَلَوْلا فَضْلُ اللهِ عَلَيْكُمْ ورحمته. وقال الكعبي: لا يضاف إلى الله إلا الحسن الجميل، ثم زعم في إضافة الطاعات إليه أنه وجه الأمر.. وأي حسن في ذلك، وقد بينا ما يدخل على ذلك. وزعم أنه لا تضاف إليه الشرور؛ لأنه نهى عنها، ولا تضاف إليه للشكر. قال الفقيه رحمه الله: وكذلك عندنا لا يضاف إليه لما بينا أن وجه الإضافة، ولا وجه في ذلك. ثم قال: قول المسلمين: الخير والشر من الله إنما أرادوا مخالفة قول الزنادقة. وأما فعل العباد لم يخطر ببالهم، بل قال الله: من عمل الشيطان. قال الفقيه رحمه الله: مما ذكر من قول المسلمين فهو كذب، بل يقولون: قدر الخير والشر من الله، وقدر الشر ليس هو الشر، ولا كان القول في شأن الزنادقة لكان إذا قبيح إضافة الشر إلى الحكيم العليم، بل [من] فعله الشر فهو شرير، وسَن فعله الإفساد فهو مفسد. وقوله: لم يخطر ببالهم، كذب، بل لا يخطر خصوص الذي ذكر، ولا قوة إلا بالله. ثم قال: فإن قيل: لا أقول الكفر من الله من جهة الأمر، ولكن نقول من جهة الخلق. قال: الأمر دون الفعل.
Then we and the Mu'tazila agree that nothing of creation or His acts is attributed to Allah except from the aspect that does not imply ugliness in names; it is right to deny that from Him. And from this arise issues: One of them is the aspect of attributing what is attributed to Allah of good things, that they are from Allah. The Mu'tazila said: It is attributed to Him by command, call to it, and strengthening it. And we said: This is from attribution, and even if it is good, this is not intended by attribution when mentioning actions, but rather the intended is gratitude and praise to Him when actions are mentioned. And the first may be permitted, but this is more appropriate; because in terms of command, call, and strengthening, the believer and disbeliever are equal, while in terms of gratitude and praise they differ. And what clarifies that is the permissibility of the absolute statement that faith is from Allah's blessings and favors, and that the believer has been favored by Allah, and that were it not for Allah's grace he would not have prospered, and he would have touched a great punishment. From this aspect, it is not attributed to Allah concerning the disbeliever. And if actions are not mentioned, then it is by command. And Allah is the one who grants success. And for this reason, Allah rebuked those who said about the altered book that it is from Allah, and by their attributions and the like, that they claimed command thereby, so Allah absolved Himself of that and informed that it is from the work of Satan, and that they said that out of envy from themselves, and there is no power except with Allah. And it is also not permissible to attribute the act by way of command, because there is nothing in it but obligation, and in that are great burdens that are not attributed to Him by that, but rather from the aspect of praise and gratitude as He said: 'Allah confers favor upon you,' and He said: 'Were it not for the grace of Allah upon you and His mercy.' And al-Ka'bi said: Nothing is attributed to Allah except the good and beautiful. Then he claimed regarding attributing acts of obedience to Him that it is by way of command—and what good is in that? And we have shown what enters upon that. And he claimed that evils are not attributed to Him because He forbade them, and they are not attributed to Him for gratitude. Al-Faqih (may Allah have mercy on him) said: Likewise, according to us, it is not attributed to Him because we have shown that the aspect of attribution, and there is no aspect in that. Then he said: The saying of the Muslims: 'Good and evil are from Allah'—they only intended to oppose the saying of the heretics. As for the actions of servants, it did not occur to them, rather Allah said: 'from the work of Satan.' Al-Faqih (may Allah have mercy on him) said: What he mentioned from the saying of the Muslims is a lie; rather they say: Allah decreed good and evil, and the decree of evil is not evil itself. And even if the statement was concerning heretics, it would be ugly to attribute evil to the Wise, All-Knowing; rather whoever does evil is evil, and whoever does corruption is a corruptor. And his statement: 'It did not occur to them' is a lie; rather what specifically occurred to them is not what he mentioned, and there is no power except with Allah. Then he said: If it is said: I do not say disbelief is from Allah by way of command, but I say by way of creation. He said: The command is below the act.
Source pages p. 909

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the Mu'tazilite position on how to attribute good actions to Allah. It begins by establishing agreement that nothing ugly is attributed to Allah. Then it presents the issue: Mu'tazila say good actions are attributed to Allah by command, call, and strengthening. Maturidi argues that the proper basis is gratitude (shukr) and praise (hamd), because command and strengthening apply equally to believer and disbeliever, while gratitude distinguishes the believer. He gives the example of faith being a blessing from Allah. He also uses the Quranic rebuke of those who falsely attributed a book to Allah. Then he refutes al-Ka'bi's claim that only good is attributed to Allah, showing that command alone is insufficient. Then al-Faqih rejects the claim that Muslims only meant to oppose heretics by saying 'good and evil from Allah,' clarifying that they mean decree (qadr), not that evil is directly from Allah in an ugly sense. Finally, an objection is raised that disbelief is from Allah by creation, not command, and the response is that command is below the action (i.e., creation encompasses everything, but attribution by command is not appropriate).

Key Terms
الإضافة
الأمر
الدعاء
التقوية
الشكر
الحمد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Attributing actions by command is always sufficient and correct.
Correction: Command alone does not distinguish believers; gratitude is the proper basis for good deeds.

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi, why is attributing good actions to Allah by command alone insufficient?
A) Because command implies ugliness
B) Because command and strengthening apply equally to believers and disbelievers
C) Because Allah does not command good
D) Because only gratitude is valid

Key Takeaway
Maturidi teaches that good deeds are attributed to Allah by gratitude and praise, not just by command, because gratitude distinguishes believers.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you succeed in a good deed, do you inwardly credit your own will and effort, or do you immediately feel gratitude to Allah for enabling you? Which response actually reflects the Maturidi teaching, and what might that reveal about your heart?
?
If attributing by gratitude distinguishes believers from disbelievers, what does your daily reaction to your own good actions say about your faith? Are you more like a believer who thanks, or like one who simply sees it as a command fulfilled?
?
Consider a recent blessing you received – like health or success. Did you see it as something Allah commanded to exist, or as a personal favor from Him? How would your relationship with Him change if you truly saw every good thing as a gift to be grateful for, not just a command?

Refuting al-Ka'bi: Good and Evil by Decree
Maturidi refutes al-Ka'bi and clarifies the meaning of 'good and evil from Allah'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Maturidi refutes al-Ka'bi's claim that only good is attributed to Allah, and clarifies that 'good and evil from Allah' refers to divine decree, not direct attribution.

Core Idea
Evil is attributed to Allah only by decree, not by direct action or command.

This passage continues the debate, focusing on evil. Al-Ka'bi claimed only good is attributed to Allah. Maturidi refutes this by showing that command alone is insufficient and that the Muslim saying 'good and evil from Allah' refers to decree, not direct creation of evil. The passage ends with an objection about disbelief by creation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify the opponents
The passage refutes al-Ka'bi and others. Note the Quranic example and argument against command.
The passage is long; read the translation carefully.
2
Understand the argument against command
Notice that attributing by command implies obligation and burden, which is not suitable for Allah.
3
Grasp the clarification on 'good and evil from Allah'
Al-Faqih explains that this means decree (qadr), not direct attribution of evil actions.
The decree of evil is not evil itself.
4
Follow the objection and response
The objection says disbelief is from Allah by creation, not command. The response is that command is below the act.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم نتفق والمعتزلة أن الله تعالى لا يضاف إليه شيء من الخلق أو أفعاله إلا من الوجه الذي لا يوهم القبح في الأسماء، ذلك فحقه أن ينفى عنه ذلك ويخرج على هذا مسائل: إحداها في وجه إضافة ما أضيف إلى الله من الخيرات، إنها من الله. قالت المعتزلة: يضاف إليه من أمر ودعا إليها وقوى عليها. وقلنا نحن: هذا من الإضافة، وإن كان حسنا فلا هذا يُراد بالإضافة إليه عند ذكر الأفعال، ولكن المراد الشكر والحمد له إذا ذكرت الأفعال. وقد يجوز الأول وهذا أولى؛ لأنه من حيث الأمر والدعاء والتقوية اشترك فيه المؤمن والكافر، ومن جهة الشكر والحمد يختلف، ومما يبين ذلك جواز القول المطلق: إن الإيمان نعم الله ومننه، وإن المؤمن قد أنعم الله عليه ومن، وأنه لولا فضل الله ما ذكى، ولمسه عذاب عظيم. ومن هذا الوجه لا يضاف إلى الله في الكافر، وإذا لم يذكر الأفعال فعلى الأمر، والله الموفق. ولهذا طعن الله من قال بالكتاب المبدل إنه من عند الله وبإضافتهم ونحوه، إنهم ادعوا الأمر بذلك، فبرأ الله نفسه عن ذلك، وأخبر أن ذلك من عمل الشيطان، وأنهم قالوا ذلك حسدا من عند أنفسهم، ولا قوة إلا بالله. ولا يجوز أيضا الفعل من حيث الأمر؛ لأنه ليس فيه إلا الالزام، وفي ذلك مؤن عظيمة لا يضاف إليه بذلك، بل من جهة الحمد والشكر كما قال: الله يَمُنُّ عَلَيْكُمْ، وقال: فَلَوْلا فَضْلُ اللهِ عَلَيْكُمْ ورحمته. وقال الكعبي: لا يضاف إلى الله إلا الحسن الجميل، ثم زعم في إضافة الطاعات إليه أنه وجه الأمر.. وأي حسن في ذلك، وقد بينا ما يدخل على ذلك. وزعم أنه لا تضاف إليه الشرور؛ لأنه نهى عنها، ولا تضاف إليه للشكر. قال الفقيه رحمه الله: وكذلك عندنا لا يضاف إليه لما بينا أن وجه الإضافة، ولا وجه في ذلك. ثم قال: قول المسلمين: الخير والشر من الله إنما أرادوا مخالفة قول الزنادقة. وأما فعل العباد لم يخطر ببالهم، بل قال الله: من عمل الشيطان. قال الفقيه رحمه الله: مما ذكر من قول المسلمين فهو كذب، بل يقولون: قدر الخير والشر من الله، وقدر الشر ليس هو الشر، ولا كان القول في شأن الزنادقة لكان إذا قبيح إضافة الشر إلى الحكيم العليم، بل [من] فعله الشر فهو شرير، وسَن فعله الإفساد فهو مفسد. وقوله: لم يخطر ببالهم، كذب، بل لا يخطر خصوص الذي ذكر، ولا قوة إلا بالله. ثم قال: فإن قيل: لا أقول الكفر من الله من جهة الأمر، ولكن نقول من جهة الخلق. قال: الأمر دون الفعل.
Then we and the Mu'tazila agree that nothing of creation or His acts is attributed to Allah except from the aspect that does not imply ugliness in names; it is right to deny that from Him. And from this arise issues: One of them is the aspect of attributing what is attributed to Allah of good things, that they are from Allah. The Mu'tazila said: It is attributed to Him by command, call to it, and strengthening it. And we said: This is from attribution, and even if it is good, this is not intended by attribution when mentioning actions, but rather the intended is gratitude and praise to Him when actions are mentioned. And the first may be permitted, but this is more appropriate; because in terms of command, call, and strengthening, the believer and disbeliever are equal, while in terms of gratitude and praise they differ. And what clarifies that is the permissibility of the absolute statement that faith is from Allah's blessings and favors, and that the believer has been favored by Allah, and that were it not for Allah's grace he would not have prospered, and he would have touched a great punishment. From this aspect, it is not attributed to Allah concerning the disbeliever. And if actions are not mentioned, then it is by command. And Allah is the one who grants success. And for this reason, Allah rebuked those who said about the altered book that it is from Allah, and by their attributions and the like, that they claimed command thereby, so Allah absolved Himself of that and informed that it is from the work of Satan, and that they said that out of envy from themselves, and there is no power except with Allah. And it is also not permissible to attribute the act by way of command, because there is nothing in it but obligation, and in that are great burdens that are not attributed to Him by that, but rather from the aspect of praise and gratitude as He said: 'Allah confers favor upon you,' and He said: 'Were it not for the grace of Allah upon you and His mercy.' And al-Ka'bi said: Nothing is attributed to Allah except the good and beautiful. Then he claimed regarding attributing acts of obedience to Him that it is by way of command—and what good is in that? And we have shown what enters upon that. And he claimed that evils are not attributed to Him because He forbade them, and they are not attributed to Him for gratitude. Al-Faqih (may Allah have mercy on him) said: Likewise, according to us, it is not attributed to Him because we have shown that the aspect of attribution, and there is no aspect in that. Then he said: The saying of the Muslims: 'Good and evil are from Allah'—they only intended to oppose the saying of the heretics. As for the actions of servants, it did not occur to them, rather Allah said: 'from the work of Satan.' Al-Faqih (may Allah have mercy on him) said: What he mentioned from the saying of the Muslims is a lie; rather they say: Allah decreed good and evil, and the decree of evil is not evil itself. And even if the statement was concerning heretics, it would be ugly to attribute evil to the Wise, All-Knowing; rather whoever does evil is evil, and whoever does corruption is a corruptor. And his statement: 'It did not occur to them' is a lie; rather what specifically occurred to them is not what he mentioned, and there is no power except with Allah. Then he said: If it is said: I do not say disbelief is from Allah by way of command, but I say by way of creation. He said: The command is below the act.
Source pages p. 909

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the Mu'tazilite position on how to attribute good actions to Allah. It begins by establishing agreement that nothing ugly is attributed to Allah. Then it presents the issue: Mu'tazila say good actions are attributed to Allah by command, call, and strengthening. Maturidi argues that the proper basis is gratitude (shukr) and praise (hamd), because command and strengthening apply equally to believer and disbeliever, while gratitude distinguishes the believer. He gives the example of faith being a blessing from Allah. He also uses the Quranic rebuke of those who falsely attributed a book to Allah. Then he refutes al-Ka'bi's claim that only good is attributed to Allah, showing that command alone is insufficient. Then al-Faqih rejects the claim that Muslims only meant to oppose heretics by saying 'good and evil from Allah,' clarifying that they mean decree (qadr), not that evil is directly from Allah in an ugly sense. Finally, an objection is raised that disbelief is from Allah by creation, not command, and the response is that command is below the action (i.e., creation encompasses everything, but attribution by command is not appropriate).

Key Terms
الأمر
الإلزام
الشكر
الحمد
قدر الخير والشر
الخلق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Good and evil are both directly created by Allah in the same sense.
Correction: Evil is decreed by Allah, but the act of evil is not attributed to Him; the decree of evil is not evil itself.

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi, what does the Muslim saying 'good and evil are from Allah' mean?
A) Allah directly creates both good and evil actions
B) It refers to divine decree, not direct attribution of evil
C) Only good is from Allah
D) Evil is from Satan, not Allah

Key Takeaway
Maturidi clarifies that evil is attributed to Allah only by decree, not by direct action, and that command alone is insufficient for attribution.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you face a tragedy or witness evil, do you truly believe that Allah's decree of that evil is not evil itself? Does your heart sometimes blame Allah for the evil you experience, even subtly? What verse or statement from this lesson can you memorize to remind yourself of the correct perspective when trials come?
?
In your own life, do you attribute your sins and failures to 'Allah's will' as an excuse to avoid taking responsibility? How can the distinction between decree and direct act help you accept accountability while still trusting in Allah's plan?
?
Al-Ka'bi wanted to protect Allah's honor by only attributing good to Him. But the truth is deeper—Allah's decree includes evil, yet He remains far above any evil. Does your heart find peace in this truth, or does it still struggle? What concrete step will you take this week to increase your trust in Allah's wisdom even in difficult circumstances?

Attributing Actions to God: Command or Grace?
Maturidi refutes attributing actions to God from the perspective of command and rejects Al-Ka'bi's view.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Maturidi argues that actions are attributed to God from the perspective of praise and gratitude, not command, and how this refutes Al-Ka'bi's position.

Core Idea
Actions are attributed to God by grace, not by command or obligation.

Maturidi confronts a key theological question: how are actions attributed to God? He argues against attributing actions based on God's command, because command implies obligation, which is unfitting. Instead, he roots attribution in praise and gratitude. This lesson explores his argument and its critique of Al-Ka'bi's view.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the Quranic references and the critique of Al-Ka'bi.
2
Identify the Quranic basis
The passage begins with God criticizing those who claim an altered book is from Him. Understand how this establishes that actions are not automatically from God just because they involve a command.
3
Grasp the argument against command
The author argues that command (al-amr) entails only obligation (al-ilzam), which would impose great burdens on God. Therefore, actions cannot be attributed to Him from that perspective.
Contrast this with the perspective of praise and gratitude (al-hamd wa al-shukr).
4
Examine the critique of Al-Ka'bi
Al-Ka'bi claims only good and beautiful things are attributed to God, yet he attributes acts of obedience by way of command. The author questions the consistency and validity of this view.
5
Reflect on the conclusion
The faqih concludes that for the author's school, actions are not attributed to God because there is no valid aspect for such attribution. Consider why this matters for understanding God's relationship to human actions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولهذا طعن الله من قال بالكتاب المبدل إنه من عند الله وبإضافتهم ونحوها، إنهم ادعوا الأمر بذلك، فبرأ الله نفسه عن ذلك، وأخبر أن ذلك من عمل الشيطان، وأنهم قالوا ذلك حسدا من عند أنفسهم، ولا قوة إلا بالله وبلى ولا يجوز أيضا الفعل من حيث الأمر؛ لأنه ليس فيه إلا الإلزام، وفي ذلك مؤن عظيمة لا يضاف إليه بذلك، بل من جهة الحمد والشكر كما قال: اللهُ يَمُنُّ عَلَيْكُمْ، وقال: فَلَوْلا فَضْلُ اللهِ عَلَيْكُمْ ورحمته ت عمده، وقال الكعبي: لا يضاف إلى الله إلا الحسن الجميل، ثم زعم في إضافة الطاعات إليه أنه وجه الأمر.. وأي حسن في ذلك، وقد بينا ما يدخل على ذلك. وزعم أنه لا تضاف إليه الشرور؛ لأنه نهى عنها، ولا تضاف إليه للشكر من قال الفقيه رحمه الله: وكذلك عندنا لا يضاف إليه لما بينا أن وجه الإضافة، ولا وجه في ذلك.
And because of this God criticized whoever said of the altered book that it is from God, and because of their attribution [of it] and the like, that they claimed the command for that, so God absolved Himself of that, and informed that that is from the work of Satan, and that they said that out of envy from themselves, and there is no power except by God. And also it is not permissible [to attribute] the action from the perspective of command, because there is nothing in it except obligation, and in that are great burdens not attributable to Him by that, but from the aspect of praise and gratitude as He said: 'God bestows favor upon you' and He said: 'Were it not for God's favor upon you and His mercy...' And Al-Ka'bi said: Nothing is attributed to God except the good and beautiful, then he claimed that in attributing acts of obedience to Him it is from the aspect of command. And what beauty is in that? And we have explained what enters upon that. And he claimed that evils are not attributed to Him because He forbade them, and they are not attributed to Him for gratitude. The faqih (may God have mercy on him) said: Likewise with us, it is not attributed to Him because we have explained that the aspect of attribution [is otherwise], and there is no aspect in that.
Source pages p. 910

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of those who attribute actions to God based on the perspective of command (al-amr) and of Al-Ka'bi's position that only good and beautiful things are attributed to God. The author begins by noting that God criticized those who claim that an altered book is from God, as they are merely claiming it by command, but God absolves Himself and states it is from Satan's work and their own envy. This establishes that actions are not to be attributed to God merely because they involve a command. Then the author argues that attributing actions to God from the perspective of command is not permissible because command entails only obligation (ilzam), which would impose great burdens (mu'an 'azima) on God, which is not appropriate. Instead, actions are attributed to God from the perspective of praise and gratitude (al-hamd wa al-shukr), citing Quranic verses about God's favor. The author then critiques Al-Ka'bi, who says only good and beautiful is attributed to God, yet claims that acts of obedience are attributed to God by way of command—questioning what 'beauty' there is in that. Al-Ka'bi also claims evils are not attributed to God because He forbade them and they are not attributed for gratitude. The faqih concludes: for us (the author's school), actions are not attributed to God for the reasons given, as there is no valid aspect for such attribution.

Key Terms
الأمر (al-amr)
الحمد والشكر (al-hamd wa al-shukr)
الإلزام (al-ilzam)
الحسن الجميل (al-hasan al-jamil)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that God's command entails His direct attribution of all commanded actions.
Correction: Maturidi clarifies that command implies obligation, which is not attributable to God. Instead, actions are attributed through grace and gratitude.

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi, from which perspective can actions be attributed to God?
A) From the perspective of command
B) From the perspective of praise and gratitude
C) From the perspective of creation
D) From the perspective of obligation

Key Takeaway
Actions are attributed to God through His grace and for praise, not because of command or obligation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you attribute a good deed you do to God, do you think of it as a command you fulfilled, or as a grace He bestowed? How does this distinction change your sense of gratitude and humility?
?
Al-Ka'bi said only good and beautiful should be attributed to God, but the author asks, 'What beauty is in that?' regarding command. Have you ever felt that God 'owes' you something because you obeyed? How does this lesson expose that pride, and what would it take for you to see every act of obedience as a gift?
?
This passage refutes attributing burdens to God. Examine your heart: Do you ever subconsciously think that your worship is a favor to God, or that He is obligated to reward you? How would your relationship with Him change if you truly internalized that everything is from His grace?

Divine Attributes

Only Praiseworthy Things Are Attributed to God
Maturidi summarizes the criterion for attributing praiseworthy things to God.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Maturidi principle that only praiseworthy meanings—such as those of glorification, gratitude, blessings, or command—may be attributed to God, and that mere creation does not justify attribution.

Core Idea
Only praise-worthy meanings, not mere creation, justify attributing things to God.

This passage from Imam Maturidi's Kitab al-Tawhid lays down a fundamental rule for divine attribution. It explains that although God creates everything, we cannot attribute everything to Him; only those things that carry a praiseworthy meaning—such as glorification, gratitude, blessings, or command—are attributed. This principle protects the purity of our conception of God.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and its translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the English translation. Notice the examples and the logical progression.
2
Identify the four valid manners of attribution
Look for the phrase 'يخرج مخرج التعظيم أو مخرج الشكر أو مخرج ذكر نعمه أو أمره'. These are the only acceptable bases.
3
Understand the summary principle
The passage summarizes that God's actions are based on justice or grace, and that even things not actually His actions can be attributed if they imply a praiseworthy meaning.
4
Apply the principle to the example
Why is 'O Creator of impurities' not said, even though God creates them? Reflect on the praiseworthy criterion.
This links back to the learning objective.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكذلك عند الناس لا يقال: يا خالق الخبائث والأنجاس ونحو ذلك، وإن كان هو في الحقيقة لكل شيء خالقا، فمثله الذي ذكرنا. وأصل ذلك إنه يضاف إلى الله تعالى كل ما كانت الإضافة إليه تخرج مخرج التعظيم أو مخرج الشكر أو مخرج ذكر نعمه أو أمره، وما خرج على غير ذلك لا يضاف إليه، وإن كان في الحقيقة خلقه، ولا قوة إلا بالله. وجملة ذلك إن الله يوصف بفعله، وهو خارج على معنى العدل أو الفضل في الحقيقة، وربما يضاف إليه ما ليس في الحقيقة فعله أو صفته، فإن كان يقتضي معنى محمودا جاز ذلك؛ لما نيل ذلك بإنعامه وأفضاله، وإن لم يكن لم
And likewise among people it is not said: 'O Creator of impurities and filth' and the like, even though He is in reality the Creator of everything. So the like of that is what we mentioned. The basis of that is that God Almighty is attributed with everything whose attribution to Him comes out in the manner of glorification (ta'ẓīm), or in the manner of gratitude (shukr), or in the manner of mentioning His blessings (ni'am) or His command (amr). And whatever comes out otherwise is not attributed to Him, even if it is in reality His creation. And there is no power except by God. The summary of that is that God is described by His action, which in reality is based on the meaning of justice ('adl) or grace (faḍl). And sometimes what is not in reality His action or attribute is attributed to Him, if it implies a praiseworthy meaning (ma'nā maḥmūd), it is permissible because that is attained by His bestowal and grace. And if not, then not.
Source pages p. 911

Commentary
This passage is a summary conclusion that establishes a clear principle for what can and cannot be attributed to God. The author begins with an example: people do not say 'O Creator of impurities and filth' even though God is the Creator of everything. This illustrates that mere creation does not justify attribution. The principle (aṣl) is that everything attributed to God must come out in one of four manners: glorification (ta'ẓīm), gratitude (shukr), mentioning His blessings (dhikr ni'am), or His command (amr). Anything else is not attributed to Him, even if He truly created it. The author then summarizes (jumla dhālika): God is described by His action, which in reality is based on justice ('adl) or grace (faḍl). This means God's actions are either just or gracious. Moreover, sometimes what is not actually His action or attribute is attributed to Him if it implies a praiseworthy meaning (ma'nā maḥmūd), because such attribution is derived from His bestowal (in'ām) and grace (afḍāl). If it does not imply a praiseworthy meaning, it should not be attributed to Him. The passage ends abruptly with 'if not, then not' (wa in lam yakun lam), likely meaning 'if not, then it is not permissible'. This establishes a strict criterion for divine attribution: only that which is praiseworthy and aligns with glorification, gratitude, blessings, or command may be attributed to God.

Key Terms
التعظيم (al-ta'ẓīm)
الشكر (al-shukr)
النعم (al-ni'am)
الأمر (al-amr)
العدل (al-'adl)
الفضل (al-faḍl)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Since God creates all things, we can call Him 'Creator of evil' or 'Creator of filth'.
Correction: Attribution is based on praiseworthy meaning, not mere creation. Only attributes that express glorification, gratitude, blessings, or command are permissible.

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT a valid manner for attributing something to God according to the passage?
A) Glorification
B) Gratitude
C) Mention of blessings
D) Mere creation

Key Takeaway
Only praiseworthy meanings—such as glorification, gratitude, blessings, or command—may be attributed to God, even though He creates everything.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you find yourself complaining about a difficulty in your life, do you realize that you might be attributing something negative to God? How can you turn that complaint into a statement of glorification or gratitude?
?
Think of a time you said 'Why did God do this to me?' about something painful. How does this lesson challenge you to rephrase that thought in a way that only praises God?
?
If you truly committed to only attributing praiseworthy meanings to God, what would change in your daily conversation, your prayers, and your inner thoughts? Write one specific intention to implement today.

The Qadariyya Claim and Maturidi's Refutation by Inconsistency
Maturidi presents the Qadariyya claim and offers a direct logical refutation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Qadariyya claim that misguidance is only by trial and abandonment, and Maturidi's first refutation showing its inconsistency.

Core Idea
Maturidi exposes the Qadariyya's own logic as self-contradictory.

The Qadariyya (Mu'tazila) argued that misguidance cannot be directly created by Allah but only through trial and abandonment, while good deeds are by command and strengthening. Maturidi immediately points out the inconsistency: if their reasoning were sound, then bringing people out of light into darkness (misguidance) should be attributed to Allah exactly as bringing them out of darkness into light is. This lesson presents that initial exchange and the question about prohibition.

Guided Path
1
Read the Qadariyya claim carefully.
Understand their distinction between good and evil attributions: good by command/strengthening, evil by trial/abandonment.
2
Follow Maturidi's parallel argument.
Notice how he applies the same logic (command/strengthening) to both good and evil, showing that if it works for one, it must work for the other, leading to inconsistency.
3
Examine the additional argument from prohibition.
Maturidi asks: if Allah forbids evil, why is it still attributed to Him in the Quran? This sets up the need for a consistent principle.
Think about how forbidding something does not negate its creation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال الفقيه رحمه الله : قالت القدرية : فيما أضيف إلى الله الإضلال والإزاغة و صرف القلوب فما قال : صَرَفَ اللهُ قلوبهم ، ونحو ذلك ، إن ذلك كان بالمحنة والتخلية ونحو ذلك ، وفى الخيرات بالأمر والتقوية ونحو ذلك ، ولو كان بالذى قالوا يضاف إليه الإخراج من النور إلى الظلمات كما أضيف إليه الإخراج الظلمات إلى النور عندهم بالأمر والتقوية ، إذ صارت علة الإضافة في الخير إليه الأمر والتقوية ، وذكر الهداية ، وكل ذكر يقابل ما ذكر ؛ إذ الأمر والتقوية هما المحنة وفيها التخلية ، فإذا استقام ذا ، ولم يستقم الآخر بان إن في ذا معنى ليس في الآخر. مع ما زعمت القدرية إن الشرور لا تضاف إليه ؛ لأنه نهي عنها ، فقد نهى عن الضلال والغواية والزيغ ، فليم أضيفت إليه ؟ والله الموفق. وقالوا فى الإضلال بالتسمية ، وذلك فاسد ؛ لما وجد من غيره ولم يضف إليه ، ولما ليس فى التسمية فضل حكمة يذكر فى موضع الوصف بالغنى والسلطان كقوله تعالى : " مَنْ يَشَا اللهُ يُضْلِلْهُ وَمَنْ يَشَأْ يَجْعَلُهُ عَلَى صِرَاطٍ مُسْتَقِيم" ، وذلك في موضع القوة والسلطان ، وبالله نستعين. والأصل في هذا كله عندنا أن الله إذ هو موصوف بفعله ، ومعنى فعله خلقه أولى ، متفضلا فى فعله أو عادلا ، لا يخلو وصف فعله عن هذين ، وحقيقته عن الأول، فصار بأى وجه أضيف إليه من طريق فعله محقق له معنى خلقه ، ولو ذكر ذا فى الإضلال وما ذكر في الطبع وغيره لم يحتمل شيء من تمويهات المعتزلة ، فكذلك إذ ذلك معنى فعله ، والله الموفق.
The jurist, may Allah have mercy on him, said: The Qadariyya said regarding what is attributed to Allah of misguidance, leading astray, and turning of hearts—such as His saying 'Allah turned their hearts'—that that was through trial and abandonment and the like, and regarding good deeds through command and strengthening and the like. And if it were as they claimed, then the bringing out from light into darkness would also be attributed to Him just as the bringing out from darkness into light is attributed to Him by command and strengthening, since the reason for attribution to Him of good is command and strengthening, and mention of guidance, and every mention corresponds to what is mentioned; for command and strengthening are trial, and in it is abandonment. So if this is consistent, and the other is not consistent, it is clear that in this there is a meaning not in the other. Along with the Qadariyya's claim that evils are not attributed to Him because He forbade them, and He forbade misguidance, error, and deviation, so why are they attributed to Him? And Allah is the Grantor of success. And they said regarding misguidance that it is by naming, and that is invalid; because it is found from others and is not attributed to them, and because there is no merit of wisdom in naming to be mentioned in the context of ascription of wealth and authority, as His saying: 'Whomever Allah wills He leads astray, and whomever He wills He sets on a straight path,' and that is in the context of power and authority. And Allah we seek help. The principle in all of this with us is that Allah, when He is described by His action, and the meaning of His action is His creation initially, whether He is gracious in His action or just, the description of His action is not free from these two, and its reality comes from the first. So by whichever aspect it is attributed to Him from the path of His action, it is verified for Him the meaning of His creation. And if this were mentioned regarding misguidance and what is mentioned regarding nature and other things, it would not bear any of the obfuscations of the Mu'tazila. Likewise, since that is the meaning of His action, and Allah is the Grantor of success.
Source pages p. 912

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the Qadariyya (Mu'tazila) argument that misguidance and evil cannot be directly attributed to Allah. The author first presents their claim: they interpret verses like 'Allah turned their hearts' as referring to trial and abandonment, not direct creation, while good things are attributed to Allah by command and strengthening. The refutation proceeds by a parallel argument: if their logic were sound, then bringing out from light to darkness (misguidance) should also be attributed to Allah by the same token, since the reason they gave for good (command and strengthening) is actually a trial that includes abandonment. Thus their reasoning is inconsistent. Then the author addresses their claim that attribution is merely by naming (tasmīya), arguing it is invalid because if it were, we would attribute misguidance to others who do it, and also the verse about guidance is in the context of power and authority. Finally, the author states the foundational principle: Allah is described by His action, and the meaning of His action is His creation – whether gracious or just. Every action attributed to Him is a true creation, which refutes the Mu'tazila obfuscations.

Key Terms
القدرية
الإضلال
الإزاغة
المحنة
التخلية
الأمر
التقوية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Qadariyya believe misguidance is not attributed to Allah at all.
Correction: Maturidi argues it is attributed, but as part of His creation, consistent with His justice.

Checkpoint
According to the Qadariyya as presented in the passage, how are good deeds attributed to Allah?
A) By trial and abandonment.
B) By command and strengthening.
C) By naming.
D) By creation.

Key Takeaway
Maturidi demonstrates that the Qadariyya's own criteria for attributing good to Allah would also require attributing evil to Him, exposing their inconsistency.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you experience a trial or hardship, do you immediately distance Allah from it in your mind, like the Qadariyya did? How does Maturidi's refutation challenge you to instead see Allah's wisdom and purpose in both good and evil? What would change in your heart if you truly accepted that every trial comes from Him?
?
The Qadariyya tried to 'protect' Allah from evil by denying His role in it. Yet Maturidi shows their logic leads to inconsistency. Are there areas in your own belief where you try to 'protect' Allah from something, only to end up contradicting the Quran? Be honest: where have you resisted submitting to Allah's decree because it felt uncomfortable?
?
Maturidi points out that command and strengthening themselves are trials. Think of a time you were given a command from Allah—like praying or giving charity—and it felt like a trial. Did you attribute the strength to obey to Allah, or did you take pride in your own effort? How does knowing that even your obedience is a trial from Him change your humility and reliance on Him?

Divine Attributes
intermediate
4 min
Refutation of the Naming (Tasmīya) Argument
Maturidi refutes the claim that attribution is merely nominal.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Maturidi rejects the Qadariyya's claim that misguidance is only attributed to Allah by way of naming, not actual creation.

Core Idea
Naming without real creation would make attribution arbitrary and meaningless.

The Qadariyya proposed a second argument: perhaps misguidance is attributed to Allah only by naming (tasmīya), not by actual creation. Maturidi refutes this on two grounds: first, we do not attribute misguidance to others even though they mislead, so naming alone is insufficient; second, verses about guidance and misguidance occur in contexts of power and authority, not mere naming. This lesson examines that rebuttal.

Guided Path
1
Understand the Qadariyya's naming argument.
They claimed that when the Quran says 'Allah leads astray,' it is only a name, not a real action.
2
Follow Maturidi's first refutation.
If it were only naming, why don't we attribute misguidance to other agents like Iblis who also mislead?
3
Examine the second refutation from Quranic context.
The verse 'Whomever Allah wills He leads astray...' is in a context of power and authority, not mere naming.
Notice the terms 'wealth' and 'authority' in the Arabic.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال الفقيه رحمه الله : قالت القدرية : فيما أضيف إلى الله الإضلال والإزاغة و صرف القلوب فما قال : صَرَفَ اللهُ قلوبهم ، ونحو ذلك ، إن ذلك كان بالمحنة والتخلية ونحو ذلك ، وفى الخيرات بالأمر والتقوية ونحو ذلك ، ولو كان بالذى قالوا يضاف إليه الإخراج من النور إلى الظلمات كما أضيف إليه الإخراج الظلمات إلى النور عندهم بالأمر والتقوية ، إذ صارت علة الإضافة في الخير إليه الأمر والتقوية ، وذكر الهداية ، وكل ذكر يقابل ما ذكر ؛ إذ الأمر والتقوية هما المحنة وفيها التخلية ، فإذا استقام ذا ، ولم يستقم الآخر بان إن في ذا معنى ليس في الآخر. مع ما زعمت القدرية إن الشرور لا تضاف إليه ؛ لأنه نهي عنها ، فقد نهى عن الضلال والغواية والزيغ ، فليم أضيفت إليه ؟ والله الموفق. وقالوا فى الإضلال بالتسمية ، وذلك فاسد ؛ لما وجد من غيره ولم يضف إليه ، ولما ليس فى التسمية فضل حكمة يذكر فى موضع الوصف بالغنى والسلطان كقوله تعالى : " مَنْ يَشَا اللهُ يُضْلِلْهُ وَمَنْ يَشَأْ يَجْعَلُهُ عَلَى صِرَاطٍ مُسْتَقِيم" ، وذلك في موضع القوة والسلطان ، وبالله نستعين. والأصل في هذا كله عندنا أن الله إذ هو موصوف بفعله ، ومعنى فعله خلقه أولى ، متفضلا فى فعله أو عادلا ، لا يخلو وصف فعله عن هذين ، وحقيقته عن الأول، فصار بأى وجه أضيف إليه من طريق فعله محقق له معنى خلقه ، ولو ذكر ذا فى الإضلال وما ذكر في الطبع وغيره لم يحتمل شيء من تمويهات المعتزلة ، فكذلك إذ ذلك معنى فعله ، والله الموفق.
The jurist, may Allah have mercy on him, said: The Qadariyya said regarding what is attributed to Allah of misguidance, leading astray, and turning of hearts—such as His saying 'Allah turned their hearts'—that that was through trial and abandonment and the like, and regarding good deeds through command and strengthening and the like. And if it were as they claimed, then the bringing out from light into darkness would also be attributed to Him just as the bringing out from darkness into light is attributed to Him by command and strengthening, since the reason for attribution to Him of good is command and strengthening, and mention of guidance, and every mention corresponds to what is mentioned; for command and strengthening are trial, and in it is abandonment. So if this is consistent, and the other is not consistent, it is clear that in this there is a meaning not in the other. Along with the Qadariyya's claim that evils are not attributed to Him because He forbade them, and He forbade misguidance, error, and deviation, so why are they attributed to Him? And Allah is the Grantor of success. And they said regarding misguidance that it is by naming, and that is invalid; because it is found from others and is not attributed to them, and because there is no merit of wisdom in naming to be mentioned in the context of ascription of wealth and authority, as His saying: 'Whomever Allah wills He leads astray, and whomever He wills He sets on a straight path,' and that is in the context of power and authority. And Allah we seek help. The principle in all of this with us is that Allah, when He is described by His action, and the meaning of His action is His creation initially, whether He is gracious in His action or just, the description of His action is not free from these two, and its reality comes from the first. So by whichever aspect it is attributed to Him from the path of His action, it is verified for Him the meaning of His creation. And if this were mentioned regarding misguidance and what is mentioned regarding nature and other things, it would not bear any of the obfuscations of the Mu'tazila. Likewise, since that is the meaning of His action, and Allah is the Grantor of success.
Source pages p. 912

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the Qadariyya (Mu'tazila) argument that misguidance and evil cannot be directly attributed to Allah. The author first presents their claim: they interpret verses like 'Allah turned their hearts' as referring to trial and abandonment, not direct creation, while good things are attributed to Allah by command and strengthening. The refutation proceeds by a parallel argument: if their logic were sound, then bringing out from light to darkness (misguidance) should also be attributed to Allah by the same token, since the reason they gave for good (command and strengthening) is actually a trial that includes abandonment. Thus their reasoning is inconsistent. Then the author addresses their claim that attribution is merely by naming (tasmīya), arguing it is invalid because if it were, we would attribute misguidance to others who do it, and also the verse about guidance is in the context of power and authority. Finally, the author states the foundational principle: Allah is described by His action, and the meaning of His action is His creation – whether gracious or just. Every action attributed to Him is a true creation, which refutes the Mu'tazila obfuscations.

Key Terms
التسمية
الغنى
السلطان
القوة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That 'naming' implies no real action by Allah.
Correction: Maturidi shows that naming would be inconsistent if no real action corresponds, and the Quranic context demands real power.

Checkpoint
What is one of Maturidi's refutations of the naming argument?
A) Naming is not used in the Quran.
B) Misguidance is found from others but not attributed to them.
C) The verse about guidance is metaphorical.
D) Naming implies actual creation.

Key Takeaway
Attribution of misguidance to Allah is not mere naming but reflects His absolute power and authority.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly believe that your misguidance—every sin and failure—is ultimately willed by Allah? If so, how does that affect your sense of personal responsibility and your reliance on Him for guidance?
?
If the Qadari claim were true and misguidance were only a name, would you feel less fear of Allah? Now that you know it is real, what must change in your heart regarding your view of Allah's power and your own accountability?

The Foundational Principle: Allah's Action is His Creation
Maturidi states the foundational principle that Allah's action is His creation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's central principle that Allah's action is defined as His creation, which resolves all attributions of good and evil.

Core Idea
Every act of Allah, whether gracious or just, is a true act of creation.

After refuting the Qadariyya's specific arguments, Maturidi lays down the foundational principle of his theology: Allah is described by His action, and the meaning of His action is His creation. This applies to all attributes, whether of guidance or misguidance. This principle, he argues, cuts through all the obfuscations of the Mu'tazila. This lesson presents that principle and its implications.

Guided Path
1
Read the principle: Allah's action = His creation.
Understand that for Maturidi, when we say Allah acts, it means He creates.
2
Notice the two categories: gracious and just.
Allah's actions are either gracious (mutafaddil) or just (ʿādil); both are true creations.
This covers both guidance and misguidance.
3
Understand how this principle verifies attribution.
Every action attributed to Allah from the path of His action is verified as His creation, regardless of whether it is good or evil.
4
See the conclusion: it refutes all obfuscations.
Maturidi states that if this principle were applied, the Mu'tazila's evasions would not stand.
Think about how this principle directly counters trial, abandonment, and naming arguments.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال الفقيه رحمه الله : قالت القدرية : فيما أضيف إلى الله الإضلال والإزاغة و صرف القلوب فما قال : صَرَفَ اللهُ قلوبهم ، ونحو ذلك ، إن ذلك كان بالمحنة والتخلية ونحو ذلك ، وفى الخيرات بالأمر والتقوية ونحو ذلك ، ولو كان بالذى قالوا يضاف إليه الإخراج من النور إلى الظلمات كما أضيف إليه الإخراج الظلمات إلى النور عندهم بالأمر والتقوية ، إذ صارت علة الإضافة في الخير إليه الأمر والتقوية ، وذكر الهداية ، وكل ذكر يقابل ما ذكر ؛ إذ الأمر والتقوية هما المحنة وفيها التخلية ، فإذا استقام ذا ، ولم يستقم الآخر بان إن في ذا معنى ليس في الآخر. مع ما زعمت القدرية إن الشرور لا تضاف إليه ؛ لأنه نهي عنها ، فقد نهى عن الضلال والغواية والزيغ ، فليم أضيفت إليه ؟ والله الموفق. وقالوا فى الإضلال بالتسمية ، وذلك فاسد ؛ لما وجد من غيره ولم يضف إليه ، ولما ليس فى التسمية فضل حكمة يذكر فى موضع الوصف بالغنى والسلطان كقوله تعالى : " مَنْ يَشَا اللهُ يُضْلِلْهُ وَمَنْ يَشَأْ يَجْعَلُهُ عَلَى صِرَاطٍ مُسْتَقِيم" ، وذلك في موضع القوة والسلطان ، وبالله نستعين. والأصل في هذا كله عندنا أن الله إذ هو موصوف بفعله ، ومعنى فعله خلقه أولى ، متفضلا فى فعله أو عادلا ، لا يخلو وصف فعله عن هذين ، وحقيقته عن الأول، فصار بأى وجه أضيف إليه من طريق فعله محقق له معنى خلقه ، ولو ذكر ذا فى الإضلال وما ذكر في الطبع وغيره لم يحتمل شيء من تمويهات المعتزلة ، فكذلك إذ ذلك معنى فعله ، والله الموفق.
The jurist, may Allah have mercy on him, said: The Qadariyya said regarding what is attributed to Allah of misguidance, leading astray, and turning of hearts—such as His saying 'Allah turned their hearts'—that that was through trial and abandonment and the like, and regarding good deeds through command and strengthening and the like. And Allah is the Grantor of success. According to Maturidi, what is the meaning of Allah's action?
A) His command.

?

?

?
The Mu'tazila created obfuscations to avoid attributing certain acts directly to Allah. Are there areas in your life where you try to soften or explain away Allah's direct involvement? What are they, and how will you realign your heart with this truth starting today?

Divine Will: Between Sovereignty and Creation
Maturidi presents views on divine will from al-Husayn, al-Ka'bi, and the Mu'tazila.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the debate over divine will among early theologians centered on whether it means God's lack of compulsion or an eternal will that creates acts.

Core Idea
Divine will is either God's sovereignty or an eternal attribute of creation.

Maturidi begins by reporting the definitions of divine will given by al-Husayn and al-Ka'bi. Both define it negatively as God not being overcome. But al-Husayn extends it to the creation of acts, while the Mu'tazila deny that God creates human acts. This lesson unpacks these views and reveals that the true issue is not will itself but the creation of acts.

Guided Path
1
Read the definitions of will from al-Husayn and al-Ka'bi
Identify the core meaning each gives: al-Husayn says 'not overcome' and al-Ka'bi says 'free (mukhtar) and not overcome'.
Notice both define will via negation of subjugation.
2
Observe how al-Husayn connects will to creation of acts
He argues that since acts are created by God, God willed them as He created them. The Mu'tazila deny creation of acts, shifting the issue.
This shows the debate is about creation, not will per se.
3
Reflect on the Mu'tazilite position as reported by Maturidi
They do not affirm an eternal will; they only say God became knowing after not knowing, making Him creator.
This contrasts with al-Husayn's eternal will.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقال حسين : معنى الإرادة فى الله سبحانه أنه لم يغلب ولم يقهر، وقد أعطت المعتزلة هذا المعنى فى جميع أفعال الخلق، إنه لم يغلب ولم يقهر، فتبطل المسألة فى الإرادة، إنما بقيت في تأويل الإرادة لا غير. الحسين : إن أفعال العباد مخلوقة، فأراد خالقها كونها على ما خلقها، ومذهب المعتزلة إنها ليست بمخلوقة لله، فتكون المسألة فى خلق الأفعال لا فى الإرادة. وقال الكعبى : الارادة معناها أنه مختار غير مغلوب، فمثله في كل شيء يلزمه، ثم المعتزلة ليست تثبت لله إلى العالم سوى أن كان، ولم يكن عالم، ثم كان عالما، فصار بذلك المعنى خالقا له، مريدا على الوجه الذي ذكر. فقال حسين في أفعال العباد : إنه إذ كان ولا هذه الأفعال، ثم كانت هذه، وكانت بإرادته التي تأويلها ما وصفه وبأن خلقها بأن كان ولم تكن هى، ولا قوة إلا بالله. على أن حسينا يجعله فى الأول مريدا لكون الخلق على ما كان، وكذلك لكون كل مخلوق على ما كان بإرادته، والمعتزلة تنفى معنى الإرادة، لا تجعل غير أن كان، ولم يكن الخلق، ثم كان، فحق ذلك فيه أوجب، ولا قوة إلا بالله. وقالت المعتزلة الوعيد يأخذ من أخرجه فعله عن الإيمان، وكذلك قال حسين وجميع أهل الإرجاء إن كان من استحق بفعله زوال اسم الإيمان فهو كله في النار أبدا، ولا قوة إلا بالله. والاختلاف بين هؤلاء في ما به يخرج من الإيمان لا فى حق الوعيد، فالاحتجاج بأى الوعيد في المسألة خطأ.
Al-Husayn said: 'The meaning of will (al-irada) in Allah, exalted is He, is that He was not overcome nor subdued.' The Mu'tazila also gave this meaning for all acts of creation: that He was not overcome nor subdued. So the issue about will becomes invalid; only the interpretation of will remains, nothing else. Al-Husayn said: 'The acts of servants are created, so their Creator willed them to be as He created them.' The doctrine of the Mu'tazila is that they are not created by Allah, so the issue is about the creation of acts, not about will. Al-Ka'bi said: 'Will means that He is free (mukhtar) and not overcome.' The same applies to everything that follows from Him. Then the Mu'tazila do not affirm for Allah with respect to the world anything except that He was not, and then He was knowing, then He became knowing, so by that meaning He became its Creator, willing in the manner mentioned. So al-Husayn said concerning the acts of servants: 'He was when there were not these acts, then these acts came to be, and they came to be by His will, the interpretation of which is what He described, and by His creating them because He was and they were not.' There is no power except with Allah. Moreover, al-Husayn makes Him in the beginning willing for creation to be as it was, and likewise for every created thing to be as it was by His will. The Mu'tazila deny the meaning of will; they do not posit anything other than that He was not and creation was not, then it came to be. So that is more incumbent in that matter. And there is no power except with Allah. The Mu'tazila said: 'The threat (al-wa'id) applies to whoever is taken out of faith by his act.' Likewise al-Husayn and all the Murji'a said: 'If someone deserves by his act the removal of the name of faith, then he is entirely in the Fire forever.' There is no power except with Allah. The disagreement between these groups is about that by which one exits faith, not about the reality of the threat. So arguing based on any threat in this issue is a mistake.
Source pages p. 921

Commentary
This passage is a sustained discussion of divine will and its relation to human acts, followed by an analysis of the threat of punishment. Maturidi first reports the views of al-Husayn and al-Ka'bi. Al-Husayn defines divine will negatively as God not being overcome or subdued, and the Mu'tazila agree on that negative definition. Maturidi notes that this agreement renders the dispute over will purely verbal. Al-Husayn further states that human acts are created by God, and God wills them to be as He creates them. The Mu'tazila deny that acts are created by God, shifting the issue to the creation of acts rather than will. Al-Ka'bi defines will as God being free (mukhtar) and not overcome. Maturidi then explains the Mu'tazilite position: they affirm a minimal temporal change in God (He was not knowing, then became knowing) to account for creation. Al-Husayn counters that God existed before acts and they came to be by His will and creation. Maturidi then summarizes: al-Husayn affirms that God eternally willed creation to be as it is, while the Mu'tazila deny any eternal will and only posit temporal origination. Maturidi considers the Mu'tazilite position to be more 'incumbent' (awjab) in some sense, perhaps acknowledging its internal logic. Then the discussion turns to the threat of punishment. Both the Mu'tazila and al-Husayn (and the Murji'a) agree that one who deserves removal of the name of faith will be in Hell forever. Maturidi clarifies that the real disagreement is about what causes one to exit faith (e.g., major sins vs. denying essentials), not about the threat itself. Therefore, citing the threat (wa'id) as proof for a specific position on the status of grave sinners is a mistake, because both sides accept the threat for those who genuinely exit faith.

Key Terms
الإرادة
خلق الأفعال
المختار

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The debate over divine will is about the meaning of the word 'will' itself.
Correction: Al-Husayn shows that if both sides accept the negative definition, the real dispute becomes whether God creates human acts, not the definition of will.

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi, what do al-Husayn and the Mu'tazila agree on regarding the meaning of divine will?
A) That will means God creates all acts directly.
B) That will means God is not overcome or subdued.
C) That will is an eternal attribute distinct from creation.
D) That will is identical to God's knowledge.

Key Takeaway
The early debate on divine will ultimately hinges on whether God creates human acts, not on a shared negative definition.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you reflect on the fact that every one of your acts is either created by God or not, how does that change the way you think about your own choices and responsibilities today? Are you willing to accept full divine sovereignty over your actions, or do you feel a tension with your own sense of freedom?
?
This passage shows that even early scholars struggled to define God's will without reducing it. In what areas of your life do you find yourself trying to define God's will in your own terms, rather than submitting to His absolute sovereignty? What would it cost you to let go of that definition?
?
If the real issue behind debates on divine will is whether God creates human acts, then your deeds are either God's creation or your own independent products. Do you live as if your good deeds are a gift from God or as if they are solely your achievement? How would your humility before God change if you truly believed He creates even your ability to obey Him?

The Threat of Punishment: Where the Real Disagreement Lies
Maturidi discusses the threat of punishment and clarifies the real point of disagreement.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the controversy over the threat of Hellfire is actually a dispute about what removes a person from faith, not about the threat itself.

Core Idea
Everyone agrees the threat is real—the question is who deserves it.

Maturidi turns to the threat of punishment. Both the Mu'tazila and al-Husayn and the Murji'a agree that those who lose the name of faith are in Hell forever. However, Maturidi points out that the real disagreement is about what causes one to exit faith—major sins or denial of essentials. Citing the threat as evidence for a specific position is therefore a mistake.

Guided Path
1
Read the agreement on the threat
Both groups agree that whoever deserves removal of faith is in Hell forever. Notice the phrase 'كل من استحق بفعله زوال اسم الإيمان فهو كله في النار أبدا'.
This shows consensus on the consequence.
2
Identify Maturidi's clarification
He states that the disagreement is about 'ما به يخرج من الإيمان' (what causes one to exit faith), not about the threat itself.
This is the key analytical point.
3
Understand the methodological mistake
Arguing based on the threat alone is flawed because both sides accept it; the real dispute lies elsewhere.
Maturidi explicitly says 'الاحتجاج بأى الوعيد في المسألة خطأ'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقال حسين : معنى الإرادة فى الله سبحانه أنه لم يغلب ولم يقهر، وقد أعطت المعتزلة هذا المعنى فى جميع أفعال الخلق، إنه لم يغلب ولم يقهر، فتبطل المسألة فى الإرادة، إنما بقيت في تأويل الإرادة لا غير. الحسين : إن أفعال العباد مخلوقة، فأراد خالقها كونها على ما خلقها، ومذهب المعتزلة إنها ليست بمخلوقة لله، فتكون المسألة فى خلق الأفعال لا فى الإرادة. وقال الكعبى : الارادة معناها أنه مختار غير مغلوب، فمثله في كل شيء يلزمه، ثم المعتزلة ليست تثبت لله إلى العالم سوى أن كان، ولم يكن عالم، ثم كان عالما، فصار بذلك المعنى خالقا له، مريدا على الوجه الذي ذكر. فقال حسين في أفعال العباد : إنه إذ كان ولا هذه الأفعال، ثم كانت هذه، وكانت بإرادته التي تأويلها ما وصفه وبأن خلقها بأن كان ولم تكن هى، ولا قوة إلا بالله. على أن حسينا يجعله فى الأول مريدا لكون الخلق على ما كان، وكذلك لكون كل مخلوق على ما كان بإرادته، والمعتزلة تنفى معنى الإرادة، لا تجعل غير أن كان، ولم يكن الخلق، ثم كان، فحق ذلك فيه أوجب، ولا قوة إلا بالله. وقالت المعتزلة الوعيد يأخذ من أخرجه فعله عن الإيمان، وكذلك قال حسين وجميع أهل الإرجاء إن كان من استحق بفعله زوال اسم الإيمان فهو كله في النار أبدا، ولا قوة إلا بالله. والاختلاف بين هؤلاء في ما به يخرج من الإيمان لا فى حق الوعيد، فالاحتجاج بأى الوعيد في المسألة خطأ.
Al-Husayn said: 'The meaning of will (al-irada) in Allah, exalted is He, is that He was not overcome nor subdued.' The Mu'tazila also gave this meaning for all acts of creation: that He was not overcome nor subdued. So the issue about will becomes invalid; only the interpretation of will remains, nothing else. Al-Husayn said: 'The acts of servants are created, so their Creator willed them to be as He created them.' The doctrine of the Mu'tazila is that they are not created by Allah, so the issue is about the creation of acts, not about will. Al-Ka'bi said: 'Will means that He is free (mukhtar) and not overcome.' The same applies to everything that follows from Him. Then the Mu'tazila do not affirm for Allah with respect to the world anything except that He was not, and then He was knowing, then He became knowing, so by that meaning He became its Creator, willing in the manner mentioned. So al-Husayn said concerning the acts of servants: 'He was when there were not these acts, then these acts came to be, and they came to be by His will, the interpretation of which is what He described, and by His creating them because He was and they were not.' There is no power except with Allah. Moreover, al-Husayn makes Him in the beginning willing for creation to be as it was, and likewise for every created thing to be as it was by His will. The Mu'tazila deny the meaning of will; they do not posit anything other than that He was not and creation was not, then it came to be. So that is more incumbent in that matter. And there is no power except with Allah. The Mu'tazila said: 'The threat (al-wa'id) applies to whoever is taken out of faith by his act.' Likewise al-Husayn and all the Murji'a said: 'If someone deserves by his act the removal of the name of faith, then he is entirely in the Fire forever.' There is no power except with Allah. The disagreement between these groups is about that by which one exits faith, not about the reality of the threat. So arguing based on any threat in this issue is a mistake.
Source pages p. 921

Commentary
This passage is a sustained discussion of divine will and its relation to human acts, followed by an analysis of the threat of punishment. Maturidi first reports the views of al-Husayn and al-Ka'bi. Al-Husayn defines divine will negatively as God not being overcome or subdued, and the Mu'tazila agree on that negative definition. Maturidi notes that this agreement renders the dispute over will purely verbal. Al-Husayn further states that human acts are created by God, and God wills them to be as He creates them. The Mu'tazila deny that acts are created by God, shifting the issue to the creation of acts rather than will. Al-Ka'bi defines will as God being free (mukhtar) and not overcome. Maturidi then explains the Mu'tazilite position: they affirm a minimal temporal change in God (He was not knowing, then became knowing) to account for creation. Al-Husayn counters that God existed before acts and they came to be by His will and creation. Maturidi then summarizes: al-Husayn affirms that God eternally willed creation to be as it is, while the Mu'tazila deny any eternal will and only posit temporal origination. Maturidi considers the Mu'tazilite position to be more 'incumbent' (awjab) in some sense, perhaps acknowledging its internal logic. Then the discussion turns to the threat of punishment. Both the Mu'tazila and al-Husayn (and the Murji'a) agree that one who deserves removal of the name of faith will be in Hell forever. Maturidi clarifies that the real disagreement is about what causes one to exit faith (e.g., major sins vs. denying essentials), not about the threat itself. Therefore, citing the threat (wa'id) as proof for a specific position on the status of grave sinners is a mistake, because both sides accept the threat for those who genuinely exit faith.

Key Terms
الوعيد
الإيمان
الإرجاء

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Mu'tazila and Murji'a disagree on whether grave sinners will be punished eternally.
Correction: Maturidi shows that both groups agree on eternal punishment for those who lose the name of faith; they differ on what causes the loss.

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi, what is the real point of disagreement among the Mu'tazila, al-Husayn, and the Murji'a regarding the threat (al-wa'id)?
A) Whether the threat of Hell applies to anyone who commits a sin.
B) Whether Allah's will is eternal or temporal.
C) What specific act or condition causes a person to exit faith.
D) Whether the threat is conditional or unconditional.

Key Takeaway
Maturidi teaches that the threat of Hell is not the real point of contention; what matters is the definition of what causes someone to exit faith.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you contemplate your own sins, do you secretly believe that a single major sin might completely expel you from faith, or do you assume your general faith protects you regardless? How does Maturidi's clarification that the threat is real but the cause of exit is defined differently challenge your self-assessment today? Will you examine what you truly believe causes someone to leave faith?
?
Think of a recent religious disagreement you had. Was the real point of contention about consequences or about the underlying cause? How often do you argue about outcomes when you actually differ on criteria? This passage calls you to refocus the debate. What will you do next time to identify the real issue first?
?
If the threat of Hell is not the point of disagreement between these groups, then what is? And more personally, have you ever used fear of Hell to coerce others into agreeing with you on theological points, while ignoring the deeper definitional issues? How can you shift your own heart to prioritize truth over winning arguments?

Al-Ka'bi's Definition of Will and Mu'tazila's Rejection
Al-Ka'bi defines divine will and contrasts with Mu'tazila on creation by knowledge.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand al-Ka'bi's definition of divine will as the attribute of free choice and how the Mu'tazila denied a distinct attribute of will, reducing it to knowledge.

Core Idea
Divine will is God's free choice, not mere knowledge.

In this passage, Imam al-Maturidi reports two competing views on the nature of divine will. Al-Ka'bi defines will as the attribute by which God is a free chooser, not compelled. The Mu'tazila, however, reject this, claiming that God's will is not a separate attribute but a consequence of His knowledge. Understanding this debate is foundational for Sunni theology on the attributes.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage and translation carefully. Identify the two main positions discussed.
2
Analyze al-Ka'bi's definition
Notice how al-Ka'bi defines will as 'mukhtar ghayr maghlub' – a chooser not overcome. This links will to freedom.
3
Contrast with Mu'tazila
See how the Mu'tazila deny a distinct will, instead saying God becomes willing through knowledge. What is the implication for God's attributes?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقال الكعبى : الارادة معناها أنه مختار غير مغلوب ، فمثله في كل شيء يلزمه ، ثم المعتزلة ليست تثبت لله إلى العالم سوى أن كان ، ولم يكن عالم ، ثم كان عالما ، فصار بذلك المعنى خالقا له ، مريدا على الوجه الذي ذكر . فقال حسين في أفعال العباد : إنه إذ كان ولا هذه الأفعال ، ثم كانت هذه ، وكانت بإرادته التي تأويلها ما وصفه وبأن خلقها بأن كان ولم تكن هى ، ولا قوة إلا بالله . على أن حسينا يجعله فى الأول مريدا لكون الخلق على ما كان ، وكذلك لكون كل مخلوق على ما كان بإرادته ، والمعتزلة تنفى معنى الإرادة ، لا تجعل غير أن كان ، ولم يكن الخلق ، ثم كان ، فحق ذلك فيه أوجب ، ولا قوة إلا بالله
Al-Ka'bi said: The meaning of will (al-irada) is that He is a chooser (mukhtar) not overcome (maghlub), so the like of it in everything follows from Him. Then the Mu'tazila do not affirm for God except that He (the world) was not and He was not knowing, then He became knowing, so He became by that meaning a creator of it, willing in the manner mentioned. Husayn said concerning the actions of servants: That when He existed while these actions were not, then these actions existed, and they existed by His will whose interpretation is what He described, and by His creating them in that He existed while they were not, and there is no power except by God. And Husayn makes Him in the beginning willing for the existence of creation as it was, and likewise for the existence of every creature as it was by His will. And the Mu'tazila deny the meaning of will; they do not affirm except that He existed and creation was not, then it existed, so that right is more incumbent in Him. And there is no power except by God.
Source pages p. 922

Commentary
This passage presents two positions: al-Ka'bi's definition of divine will and the Mu'tazila's alternative view. Al-Ka'bi defines will (al-irada) as the attribute that makes God a free chooser (mukhtar) who is not overcome or compelled (ghayr maghlub). This meaning, he argues, necessarily applies to everything God does. The Mu'tazila, on the other hand, do not affirm a distinct attribute of will for God; they reduce it to a consequence of God's knowledge. They hold that before creation, God was not yet knowing the world, and once He became knowing, that very knowledge made Him a creator and willing. Husayn (likely al-Najjar or a similar figure) offers a different view on human actions: they exist by God's will, interpreted as His creative power, such that He existed before they existed, and they came to be by His will. Husayn affirms that God was always willing for creation to be as it is, and for each creature to be as it is by His will. The Mu'tazila, in contrast, deny any distinct meaning of will; they only assert that God existed while creation was not, then creation came to be, and that right (i.e., the fact of becoming creator) is more necessarily attributed to Him. The passage ends with the refrain 'there is no power except by God.'

Key Terms
الإرادة
المختار
المغلوب
المعتزلة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That al-Ka'bi denies a real attribute of will.
Correction: Al-Ka'bi actually affirms will as a distinct attribute denoting freedom, not mere knowledge.

Checkpoint
According to al-Ka'bi, what does divine will (al-irada) mean?
A) God is a chooser not overcome
B) God's knowledge of creation
C) God's power to create
D) God's decree

Key Takeaway
Al-Ka'bi affirms divine will as a distinct attribute of free choice, while the Mu'tazila reduce it to a function of knowledge.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If God's will is a distinct attribute of free choice, then every decision you make exists because He willed it. How does this confront your feeling of autonomy? Write one decision today where you must consciously submit your will to His.
?
The Mu'tazila reduce will to knowledge—making God a passive observer of what He knows. Is there an area in your life where you treat God's knowledge as mere information without letting His will transform your actions? What would it mean to let His will interrupt your plans?
?
Al-Ka'bi says God is a free chooser not overcome. In what area of your life do you act as if God's will can be overcome by your circumstances? What would it mean to trust that His will prevails even when you feel stuck?

The Verse on Shirk and Divine Forgiveness
Maturidi refutes those who misuse the verse about shirk to deny forgiveness for major sins.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Maturidi uses the verse 'Indeed, God does not forgive shirk' to argue that forgiveness for major sins is possible without repentance.

Core Idea
Even shirk can be forgiven; denying forgiveness for lesser sins is foolish.

In this passage, Imam Maturidi tackles a common misinterpretation of the Quranic verse that seems to limit forgiveness only to those who avoid shirk. He shows that the verse actually proves the opposite: forgiveness is up to God's will, not our limitations. This lesson unpacks his argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and translation once to get the overall flow.
2
Identify the two refuted positions
The passage refutes two views: those who restrict the verse's application and those who deny forgiveness for major sins without repentance.
3
Understand the logical pivot
Note that shirk itself can be forgiven through repentance; this undermines both positions.
Repentance shows forgiveness is not absolutely denied.
4
Reflect on the conclusion
Maturidi concludes that God has willed forgiveness, and rejecting that is foolish.
This upholds divine mercy.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم الله تعالى قال : إِنَّ اللهَ لَا يَغْفِرُ أَن يُشْرَكَ بِهِ ومعلوم أن الشرك قد يغفر بالتوبة ، فبطل به قول من يجعله لما قسم الكتاب ، وبطل قول من يبطل المغفرة فى الكبائر بلا توبة ؛ لأن الله جل ثناؤه جعل لنفسه مشيئة المغفرة ، وذلك فما كان فى الحكمة ، لكن دفعه سفه جل الله عن ذلك وتعالى ، ذكرت القولين جميعا .
Then God Almighty said: 'Indeed, God does not forgive that partners be associated with Him.' And it is known that shirk may be forgiven through repentance. So it invalidates by this the saying of those who make it for what the Book made clear, and it invalidates the saying of those who nullify forgiveness for major sins without repentance, because God, great and exalted, placed for Himself the will of forgiveness. And that is what was in wisdom, but its rejection is foolishness - God is exalted above that and high. I have mentioned both statements.
Source pages p. 926

Commentary
This passage refutes two positions using the verse about forgiveness of shirk. The fact that shirk itself can be forgiven through repentance shows that forgiveness is not restricted only to minor sins or only with repentance. Maturidi argues that God has willed forgiveness, and to deny that is foolish. He mentions both the view that limits the verse and the view that denies forgiveness for major sins without repentance.

Key Terms
شرك
مغفرة
توبة
مشيئة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The verse means shirk is absolutely unforgivable, so other sins are easier to forgive.
Correction: Maturidi argues that if shirk can be forgiven through repentance, then other sins can also be forgiven by God's will even without repentance.

Checkpoint
What does Maturidi argue using the verse about not forgiving shirk?
A) That shirk is never forgiven
B) That only shirk requires repentance
C) That shirk can be forgiven, so other sins can be forgiven by God's will
D) That all sins are forgiven automatically

Key Takeaway
The verse about not forgiving shirk actually supports the possibility of forgiveness for major sins through God's will.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly believe that God can forgive your greatest sins, or do you secretly think some are too big for His mercy? What would it mean for your relationship with Him if you fully trusted His will to forgive?
?
When you sin, do you rely more on your own repentance or on God's boundless will to forgive? How does this lesson challenge you to shift your reliance?
?
Have you ever fallen into the foolishness of limiting God's forgiveness—either by thinking He only forgives certain sins or that repentance is a rigid requirement? What step will you take today to repent and trust His will completely?
